  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/28969495-rebecca-davis"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1393160269i/28969495._UY100_CR8,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/28969495-rebecca-davis">Rebecca Davis</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    My take on it is that Emma was the daughter of the professor who got Vanessa pregnant when she was in college. Emma's parents split up over it, so she<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    My take on it is that Emma was the daughter of the professor who got Vanessa pregnant when she was in college. Emma's parents split up over it, so she set out to get revenge on Vanessa. She had initially gotten involved with Richard to get closer to Vanessa. But in the end she finds out that Vanessa didn't know about her mother (the professor's wife) when she was involved with her father (the professor). In other words, Vanessa didn't know she was having an affair. In addition, Emma didn't realize Richard was abusive. And she respected Vanessa for both telling her the truth about trying to get them together and about trying to save her from him. So in the end, the two meet and exchange Emma's real identity, both are left with a sense of closure.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>
</div>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This question contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a href="/questions/1283608-am-i-the-only-one-who-got-the-characters"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Am I the only one who got the characters confused?? In the beginning, it was pretty clear...Vanessa was the wife, worked at Sax and lived with Aunt Charlotte. Nellie lived with Sam until the wedding and worked with the pre school children. But later on in the book, it was like it was Vanessa talking about her best friend Sam and referring to when she used to work with the children. I'm still confused about that! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></a>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_2237708317" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2237708317" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2237708317?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=botm">botm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2237708317" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13982369892839106665"><b>I KNEW IT!</b><br/><br/>2 1/2 stars. Ugh, I'm almost as disappointed in myself as I am in this book. I don't consider myself an especially astute mystery/thriller reader. Pull out a good twist and I will probably be surprised. But here I saw the first big twist coming, and the string of twists after that left me feeling cold. Trust me to be wearing my detective glasses at the exact moment I really needed to be surprised.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34189556.The_Wife_Between_Us' title='The Wife Between Us by Greer Hendricks' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Wife Between Us</a> basically introduces itself in the blurb as a book full of twists. <i>Ass</i></span>
  <span id="freeText13982369892839106665" style="display:none"><b>I KNEW IT!</b><br /><br />2 1/2 stars. Ugh, I'm almost as disappointed in myself as I am in this book. I don't consider myself an especially astute mystery/thriller reader. Pull out a good twist and I will probably be surprised. But here I saw the first big twist coming, and the string of twists after that left me feeling cold. Trust me to be wearing my detective glasses at the exact moment I really needed to be surprised.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34189556.The_Wife_Between_Us" title="The Wife Between Us by Greer Hendricks" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wife Between Us</a> basically introduces itself in the blurb as a book full of twists. <i>Assume nothing</i>, it warns. A big chunk of the plot is fairly quiet and uneventful, which means a lot hangs on that moment of thrilling shock one should experience as the authors pull out their surprises. <b>It's not a book that survives very well on its own if you happen to figure out the truth.</b><br /><br />And I did. Or, at least, I got the first truth. The authors have this big dramatic moment where they metaphorically lift the curtain... and I was so disappointed to have worked out what was happening. The impact just wasn't there. The slow climb to what should have been a shocking climax was just a slow climb for me.<br /><br />I'll give away as little as possible. <br /><br />The book begins by alternating between the perspectives of Richard's ex-wife, Vanessa, who has been left penniless and with a drinking problem ever since their mysterious break-up, and his new and young fiancée, Nellie, who is busy making wedding plans and trying to ignore the feeling that someone is following her. Vanessa is determined to stop Richard marrying again, but how far will she go to prevent it? <br /><br />That's pretty much all I can safely tell you. <br /><br />If I'm honest, after the first twist didn't quite hit the spot, I think my attitude toward the book changed. Where before I'd been eagerly anticipating the reveals, I was now waiting, somewhat unmoved, for the twists to happen. And, of course, more and more did. It gets a little excessive after a while. BAM, twist! BAM, another twist! At one point, I stopped being shocked by the revelations because I figured something else would soon be along to tear that apart, too.<br /><br />And that very last twist? I rolled my eyes. It felt so unnecessary and kind of silly. It was already tough keeping track of what the real story was; we didn't need another shocker tagged on. Plus, the whole subplot with Maggie and Jason was boring and took up too much page time.<br /><br />Some books are full of enough tension and/or interesting characterization to make it okay if you guess what is going on, and some books pull out twists that are shocking and impressive enough that the surprise carries the story. I know for a lot of people <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34189556.The_Wife_Between_Us" title="The Wife Between Us by Greer Hendricks" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wife Between Us</a> will be, and is, the latter, but it didn't quite work for me.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13982369892839106665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2189301197" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2189301197" />
    <a title="Meredith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith"><img alt="Meredith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423329725p2/30978160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2189301197?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith">Meredith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2189301197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12401081214228023537"><b>2.5 stars<br/><br/>I know I am probably going to get beat up for this, but here goes nothing….<br/><br/><i>Secrets, lies, and a whole lot of over-the-top twists make up The Wife Between Us. This was a fun and entertaining read, but in the end it wasn’t the right book for me. </i></b><br/><br/>I loved the first half of this book--I ate up every word, and dreaded the moment when I had to put it down. I was surprised by the first twist--it threw me for a loop! <b>Seriously, I was so addicted to this book that I read it every chance I got, in</b></span>
  <span id="freeText12401081214228023537" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars<br /><br />I know I am probably going to get beat up for this, but here goes nothing….<br /><br /><i>Secrets, lies, and a whole lot of over-the-top twists make up The Wife Between Us. This was a fun and entertaining read, but in the end it wasn’t the right book for me. </i></b><br /><br />I loved the first half of this book--I ate up every word, and dreaded the moment when I had to put it down. I was surprised by the first twist--it threw me for a loop! <b>Seriously, I was so addicted to this book that I read it every chance I got, including walking to my car at night (dumb move on my end). </b><br /><br />But then as more and more twists occurred and Vanessa’s story further unraveled, I just wasn’t feeling it anymore. I grew bored as I waiting for something to happen. After her final confrontation with Richard, the remaining chapters felt superfluous. <b>And that final twist?! UGH. NOPE. Did not work for me. </b> <br /><br />I finished the final page, rolled my eyes and groaned out of frustration. What had started out with so much promise turned into a bit of a ridiculous mess that seemed more concerned with twists than substance.<br /><br />This book is receiving tons of great reviews, and many of my Goodreads friends absolutely love it. I am often overly critical when it comes to thrillers, so I would recommend that you read <i> The Wife Between Us</i> and judge for yourself!<br /><br />I would have given this one star, but bumped up my rating as I was completely captivated and entertained by the first half.<br /><br />I received a copy of this book from NetGalley and the publisher in exchange for an honest review.<br /></span>

<div id="review_2139736484" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2139736484" />
    <a title="j e w e l s" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s"><img alt="j e w e l s" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552606306p2/68216634.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2139736484?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="j e w e l s" class="user" itemprop="url" name="j e w e l s" href="/user/show/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s">j e w e l s</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s?shelf=twister-hall-of-fame">twister-hall-of-fame</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s?shelf=books-bejeweled">books-bejeweled</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2139736484" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4682228832641406072"><b>OH. MY. GOSHHHHHHHHHHH. I HAD TO ADD THIS TO MY TWISTER HALL OF FAME SHELF!</b><br/> <br/>Where to start? This is hands down the twistiest, fastest, funnest-to-read domestic suspense in ages!<br/><br/>Unreliable narrator? Check.<br/><br/>Breath taking plot twists? Check.<br/><br/>Fast turning addictive page turning? Check. check. check. check. check!<br/><br/><i>What else is there in life? </i><br/><br/>Unlike all the other domestic noir books that claim to be the next Gone Girl, THE WIFE BETWEEN US actually IS the next book that people will go crazy over. I'm so e</span>
  <span id="freeText4682228832641406072" style="display:none"><b>OH. MY. GOSHHHHHHHHHHH. I HAD TO ADD THIS TO MY TWISTER HALL OF FAME SHELF!</b><br /> <br />Where to start? This is hands down the twistiest, fastest, funnest-to-read domestic suspense in ages!<br /><br />Unreliable narrator? Check.<br /><br />Breath taking plot twists? Check.<br /><br />Fast turning addictive page turning? Check. check. check. check. check!<br /><br /><i>What else is there in life? </i><br /><br />Unlike all the other domestic noir books that claim to be the next Gone Girl, THE WIFE BETWEEN US actually IS the next book that people will go crazy over. I'm so excited, I wish it were coming out before January, because I cannot wait for you and everyone I know to read it!<br /><br />This is actually a very simple storyline, you've heard it before. Husband, wife, mistress. The difference is the clever, seamless way it is presented. Trust me, you've not ever read a story like this before. It's genius.<br /><br />I've posted a more in-depth (but NO SPOILERS) review on my blog at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://booksbejeweled.com/2018/01/09/the-wife-between-us/">https://booksbejeweled.com/2018/01/09...</a><br /><br />IMPORTANT PUBLIC ANNOUNCEMENT<br /><b>The authors just announced on Instagram that the book has already been optioned for film, by the same team at DreamWorks that brought us THE GIRL ON THE TRAIN movie.</b> So exciting!<br /><br />For now, I just want to encourage all you influential readers to try and get your hands on a copy of THE WIFE BETWEEN US. I'm grateful to the folks at Netgalley for the opportunity to read and review it months ahead of publication.<br /><br /><b>THIS BOOK IS LIT!</b></span>

<div id="review_2201515935" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2201515935" />
    <a title="Gabby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26560207-gabby"><img alt="Gabby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482222518p2/26560207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2201515935?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabby" href="/user/show/26560207-gabby">Gabby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=annoying-characters">annoying-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=over-freaking-hyped">over-freaking-hyped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=thrillers-or-mystery">thrillers-or-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=1-star-books">1-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=just-no">just-no</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=read-in-one-day">read-in-one-day</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=botm">botm</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2201515935" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5850387607597926742"><b>Warning: unpopular opinion.</b> I cannot for the life of me understand the high ratings and great reviews this book is getting. The description for this book on goodreads literally says: <i>"Discover the next blockbuster novel of suspense, and get ready for the read of your life."</i> Blockbuster novel of suspense? Did I just read the right book? Is this a joke or...?<br/><br/>This book claims to be a suspense/thriller but it's neither of those things. It's a mystery that is dragged out throughout the entire book, t</span>
  <span id="freeText5850387607597926742" style="display:none"><b>Warning: unpopular opinion.</b> I cannot for the life of me understand the high ratings and great reviews this book is getting. The description for this book on goodreads literally says: <i>"Discover the next blockbuster novel of suspense, and get ready for the read of your life."</i> Blockbuster novel of suspense? Did I just read the right book? Is this a joke or...?<br /><br />This book claims to be a suspense/thriller but it's neither of those things. It's a mystery that is dragged out throughout the entire book, that I couldn't give two fucks about honestly. I made an update around the 200 page mark where I complained that nothing interesting had even happened in the story yet and I wasn't sure if I should finish it, but I did and... god damn this book was my Everest. It took so much energy to finish this book because of how bored I was by the story. The title and the goodreads description of this book make it seem like it's going to be some crazy twisted love triangle with so many plot twists and that it's going to be so different form anything else you've ever read, but in reality it's this ridiculously annoying love triangle with a main chaarcter who is obsessed with her ex-husband and a few lame "plot twists" get thrown in along the way. The majority of this book is the main character Vanessa having flashbacks of her marriage with Richard and how "omg he was so perfect then" and "omg where did it all go wrong?" and it was so <i>boring</i>. The writing style is confusing too because I was always confused when it would randomly dive into a flashback and then randomly come back to the present. I never knew what scenes were taking place currently and what scenes were flashbacks, it was just very unorganized. <br /><br />This book attempts to make a 'plot twist' at the end of part one, which is around the 150 page mark, but it doesn't really change anything in the story. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Like omg so you're telling me Nellie is actually Vanessa the entire time, and Nellie's parts were all just flashbacks of the beginning of her marriage with Richard? Cool. Doesn't change anything and I still don't know what went wrong in their marriage. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It's not a great plot twist, and I was expecting more from the next two parts. When I finally realized what this story is about towards the end, and I realized there wouldn't be any mind blowing plot twists, I was really disappointed. At the end of the day this is just another one of those stories where <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the main character Vanessa marries a man and he turns into this crazy, abusive asshole out of nowhere, and then she tries to escape from him. I'm just really tired of the 'I married a sweet guy and he turned out to be an abusive monster' trope in mysteries. It's gotten really old for me really fast. I just assumed this story would have more to it than that. Not to mention, I was irritated with Vanessa for 99% of the story because I'm like... If Richard was so abusive and you got away, why the hell are you still obsessing over him and trying to contact them? I know she's trying to 'save Emma' or whatever but still... Especially in part one she's constantly talking about how much she misses him and how great he used to be... like I'm sorry but get the fuck over it, he's disgusting and abusive. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />I just hate that the main <i>mystery</i> happening in this story is trying to figure out what went wrong in Vanessa and Richard's marriage, and when it's finally revealed it's very obvious and basic and this mystery doesn't bring anything new to the table that we haven't seen in mysteries ten million times. I think this book tries to be clever and it just epically fails, and it was just so boring. The only good thing this book has going for it is the epilogue, which did have a plot twist that I didn't see coming - but even that did not make this book worth reading. I feel like I wasted my day off reading this, so read at your own risk. I don't recommend this.<br /><br /><b>Thank you to Book of the Month for sending me this book as one of their December selections!</b> </span>
  <a data-text-id="5850387607597926742" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2037738527" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2037738527" />
    <a title="Deanna " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15662887-deanna"><img alt="Deanna " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437589889p2/15662887.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2037738527?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deanna " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deanna " href="/user/show/15662887-deanna">Deanna </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15662887-deanna?shelf=my-favorites">my-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2037738527" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5608549930579149878">My reviews can also be seen at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpress.com/'>https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpr...</a><br/><br/>All the stars!!<br/><br/>It was the cover that first caught my eye. I loved it. And after reading the description for this novel, I couldn’t wait to read it.<br/><br/>As the book opens, a woman is unaware that someone is watching her. That someone is out to ruin her.<br/><br/><strong>
  <em>“She is oblivious to what I have done to her”</em>
</strong><br/><br/><strong>NELLIE</strong> can’t talk about the night that began with drinks and laughter, but ended with police and despair.<br/><br/>But now Nellie feels safe w</span>
  <span id="freeText5608549930579149878" style="display:none">My reviews can also be seen at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpress.com/">https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpr...</a><br /><br />All the stars!!<br /><br />It was the cover that first caught my eye. I loved it. And after reading the description for this novel, I couldn’t wait to read it.<br /><br />As the book opens, a woman is unaware that someone is watching her. That someone is out to ruin her.<br /><br /><strong>
  <em>“She is oblivious to what I have done to her”</em>
</strong><br /><br /><strong>NELLIE</strong> can’t talk about the night that began with drinks and laughter, but ended with police and despair.<br /><br />But now Nellie feels safe with Richard. He helps to keep the nightmares at bay. Richard is loving, caring, and protective. He has impeccable manners and seems to fit in anywhere and with anyone. Her friends and her mother wonder if he’s too good to be true….<br /><br /><strong>
  <em>“Her mother didn’t get it. Richard fixed everything. She’d be safe with him no matter where they lived”</em>
</strong><br /><br />But lately Nellie has been getting strange phone calls and sometimes it seems like she’s being followed. Richard tells her not to worry, but it’s starting to make her anxious.<br /><br /><strong>Nellie had come to New York to escape.</strong><br /><br />She loves her job at The Learning Ladder. It’s where she met her best friend, Samantha. She enjoys working with preschoolers, although it can be hard dealing with their insufferable parents. They love to ask personal questions, like where she’s from. But Nellie is careful not to reveal too much about her past.<br /><br /><strong>What happened to make her leave Florida? What is Nellie hiding?</strong><br /><br />Nellie doesn’t know very much about Richard’s ex. Just that they split up before he met Nellie. Richard really is the best thing that ever happened to Nellie.<br /><br /><strong>
  <em>“She’d always regret certain decisions in her life, but choosing Richard would never be one of them”</em>
</strong><br /><br /><strong>VANESSA</strong> is living at her aunt’s house. Morning is the worst time of the day because for a moment she can forget, but then reality comes crashing down around her. She imagines Richard and her replacement and what they are doing at that moment. Her aunt believes that Vanessa is the victim in all of this. But Vanessa wonders what her aunt would think if she knew the truth…if she knew what Vanessa had done.<br /><br />She wonders if she’ll ever have peace….<br /><br /><strong>“My regret is an open wound”</strong><br /><br />Vanessa now works as a sales associate at Saks. She waits on the wealthy women that she used to lunch with. Richard got the house, the cars, the money...everything. It’s like he wants to erase their relationship, to pretend like she never existed.<br /><br /><strong>
  <em>“I entered the marriage with nothing. I hadn’t worked. I hadn’t borne him children. I’d been deceitful. I hadn’t been a good wife”</em>
</strong><br /><br />It’s so easy to make assumptions. I was positive I knew what was going on but I was so wrong.<br /><br />Like the book says…<br /><br /><strong>“</strong><strong>Assume nothing”</strong><br /><br />Who is telling the truth? Who can be trusted?<br /><br />At first I found the beginning a little slow, but then I realized that the authors were trying to set the scene by giving some background. It wasn’t long before I was pulled into the story and the lives of these characters. I was so sure I knew where things were headed. I was in shock at the first twist, confused and thinking I read something wrong or missed a page. It was so unexpected ….but I loved it. I really appreciate when a story is able to blindside me like that.<br /><br /><em><strong>“The Wife Between Us”</strong> </em>is a twisted and complex psychological suspense novel. A story about marriage, friendship, betrayal, manipulation, obsession and more. A fast-paced and addictive novel that held my interest from start to finish. This story kept me on my toes guessing right up until the very end. I honestly can’t wait to read more from Greer Hendricks and Sarah Pekkanen.<br /><br />Thank you to NetGalley and St. Martin’s Press for the opportunity to read this book in exchange for my honest review.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2694493233" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2694493233" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528750408p2/9684061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2694493233?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=predictable">predictable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=suspense-mystery-thriller">suspense-mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=too-much-hype">too-much-hype</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2694493233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11657457931728776758"><i>It’s a little late now—will all the pages having been turned—but my initial decision to skip this one way back when was the <u>right</u> one.</i><br/><br/>I was pretty darn adamant about sticking to my guns—bypassing this book entirely—until I wasn’t. Some <i>anonymous girl</i> convinced me I *had* to know who <i>the wife</i> was getting between people. <br/><br/>Thank goodness for small favors though. Had I not been a hype avoider last year, no doubt, I would have succumbed to the almighty and powerful <u>F</u>ear <u>O</u>f <u>M</u>issing <u>O</u>ut and snatched up </span>
  <span id="freeText11657457931728776758" style="display:none"><i>It’s a little late now—will all the pages having been turned—but my initial decision to skip this one way back when was the <u>right</u> one.</i><br /><br />I was pretty darn adamant about sticking to my guns—bypassing this book entirely—until I wasn’t. Some <i>anonymous girl</i> convinced me I *had* to know who <i>the wife</i> was getting between people. <br /><br />Thank goodness for small favors though. Had I not been a hype avoider last year, no doubt, I would have succumbed to the almighty and powerful <u>F</u>ear <u>O</u>f <u>M</u>issing <u>O</u>ut and snatched up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34189556.The_Wife_Between_Us" title="The Wife Between Us by Greer Hendricks" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wife Between Us</a>. My discontent with this obvious and exhausting storyline (<i>aside from Part 1</i>), would have stopped me from experiencing all the thrills and chills <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/39863515.An_Anonymous_Girl" title="An Anonymous Girl by Greer Hendricks" rel="nofollow noopener">An Anonymous Girl</a> unleashed with her psychological study participation. Now that would have been an incredible shame. To date—keep in mind, as I write this review it's only early February—AAG is the only book I’ve awarded a 5-star rating in 2019. In my opinion, TWBU is nowhere near as riveting or original as the writing duo’s sophomore offering. The masses are divided on this front though, which makes perusing the reviews quite fun.<br /><br />With this debut—as both co-writers and suspense storytellers—<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2982045.Sarah_Pekkanen" title="Sarah Pekkanen" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah Pekkanen</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16935182.Greer_Hendricks" title="Greer Hendricks" rel="nofollow noopener">Greer Hendricks</a> introduce readers to two <i>very</i> different women, Vanessa and Nellie. The one person that connects them, a wealthy, successful, cardboard cutout of the perfect man, otherwise known as Richard. Vanessa is a drunk, down on her luck, barely surviving hot mess whose idiosyncrasies drive her to stalk unsuspecting Nellie. Naturally, as Richard’s former wife, Vanessa’s a bit salty that he’s moved on so quickly and poised to exchange vows with her much younger replacement. A (crazy?) sliver of my own psyche almost couldn’t blame her without having all the facts—like who left who and <u>why</u>? Well, wonder away, until you read the book for yourself. You’re not going to get any answers from me in regards to plot details. Much else would ruin what becomes a predictable trajectory. <br /><br />I’ll shout it loud and proud all day, Part 1 of 3, <i>owned</i> me in its entirety. I feverishly turned those 162-ish pages, DEVOURING that slice of the pie in one sitting. I was obsessed with finding out how Veronica’s mission was going to play out. Part 2, on the other hand, led the descent into disappointed reader territory. The thought reverberating in my mind: really, <i>that</i> uninspired twist was the BIG reveal? The authors pretty much destroyed everything that made the book so compulsively readable. To say I was over it by Part 3 is all too accurate. The culmination of the so-called surprises, entirely TOO LONG trek (50 pages could have been cut from the final draft easily), and overdone ending, found me eager to move on.<br /><br />To clarify, there was one aspect of the ending that I thought was clever and worked to tie everything together, but another that cheapened things.<br /><br />We all like what we like and can’t force it or even explain it sometimes; that’s just life. Trying to predict what your own experience might be, based on my gibberish alone probably isn’t fair. So, if something about this one sparks your interest, I’d say go for it. You never know what might happen. <br /><br /><i>*Thank you to St. Martin’s Press for furnishing a review copy.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="11657457931728776758" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2076567273" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2076567273" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2076567273?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=from-publisher-or-author">from-publisher-or-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2076567273" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1153044496508967721"><b>oooh, goodreads choice awards semifinalist for best mystery & thriller 2018! what will happen?</b><br/><br/>every time i read a review where a book is “praised” as being "compulsively readable," i roll my eyes. <br/><br/>ev. er. y. time.<br/><br/>and i don't know if this particular book has received that lazy praise-umbrella anywhere, but in general, it's one of those overused empty-calorie assessments that tells me nothing about a book but is taking up space and time where i could have been reading something more useful. which </span>
  <span id="freeText1153044496508967721" style="display:none"><b>oooh, goodreads choice awards semifinalist for best mystery &amp; thriller 2018! what will happen?</b><br><br>every time i read a review where a book is “praised” as being "compulsively readable," i roll my eyes. <br><br>ev. er. y. time.<br><br>and i don't know if this particular book has received that lazy praise-umbrella anywhere, but in general, it's one of those overused empty-calorie assessments that tells me nothing about a book but is taking up space and time where i could have been reading something more useful. which is how most karen-eyerolls are earned. and yet... i gulped this book down, i got mad when i had to pause in my reading of it to sleep, get off the train, go to work, look both ways for traffic (i read while i walk down streets), etc, and while i'm not here claiming it's the literary masterpiece that's going to change books forever, it is - dare i say??<br><br>COMPULSIVELY READABLE!<br><br>full review to come.<br><br>(from me - there are plenty of other reviews on here that are bound to be better than mine, have at 'em!) <br><br>okay, “to come” is now. <br><br>so - this book was an unsolicited bonus book that st. martin’s sent along way back when they sent me an arc of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33574211.Emma_in_the_Night" title="Emma in the Night by Wendy Walker" rel="nofollow noopener">Emma in the Night</a> for review. this arc had a plain white cover, the pub date was 7 months away, and it was written by two authors*, none of which were pushing this book to the top of my stack: i’m easily swayed by cover art, i’m always wary of books written by more than one person, and i had a mountain of arcs with closer pub dates that needed my attention. so i put this one off for a while, figuring it was just one more hastily-written book being plopped onto the neverending conveyor belt of middlebrow marriage-based psych suspense. <br><br>but nooooooo - this is probably** the best psychological suspense i read all year (and i read a few), and i liked this one more than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33574211.Emma_in_the_Night" title="Emma in the Night by Wendy Walker" rel="nofollow noopener">Emma in the Night</a>, so thank you for the unexpected treat, st. martins! <br><br>i was just being silly up there, but there really is something compulsively readable about this book. it’s a breezy, easy read, but i don’t mean that in a bad way. i’m not sure how to articulate it - it’s unchallenging without being unambitious, if that makes sense. because this had to have taken pretty rigorous plotting and outlining for all the twists and reveals to land***, so it’s damn ambitious, but it goes down like pudding. and along the way, there are a couple of lumps in the pudding - not enough to ruin the taste, but enough to make you pause and say “hmmmm,” and try to figure out what those lumps signify, and i, for one, did not figure it out until the authors wanted me to figure it out. which is exactly what i want out of a book in this genre. <br><br>so - many kudos and much gratitude to those involved in writing and editing this book. it was so much fun (where the definition of "fun" is modulated to take into account the genre standards of people being horrible to each other), and very surprising. <br><br>so no spoilers, suckers! get your own pudding! <br><br><br>* and i’m not a book snob - no one who has read as much monsterporn as i have is gonna have any judgment left in them, but i do know my own preferences, and one of the authors has published a number of books whose cover montage of “back of a woman gazing out in contemplation at the sea/the woods/some other vista” made me think they would not be aligned with my particular tastes. i prefer action to introspection in my books. <br><br>** it’s either this or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32326398.Sometimes_I_Lie" title="Sometimes I Lie by Alice Feeney" rel="nofollow noopener">Sometimes I Lie</a><br><br>*** and it’s <i>very</i> rare for them all to land in such an early arc, so give the editorial team a pizza party<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1153044496508967721" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer6306086797408918626">This is without doubt a tense psychological thriller that makes a impact. It has you wondering if what you were reading was for real, and re-reading to check. It has you questioning what you think you know and where nothing is as it seems. Vanessa Thompson is a divorced woman who is barely managing to keep herself together and her days off from her job at Saks endanger her employment. She exists in a alcoholic haze, the wine bottles in her home attest to this. Vanessa used to be married to the w</span>
  <span id="freeText6306086797408918626" style="display:none">This is without doubt a tense psychological thriller that makes a impact. It has you wondering if what you were reading was for real, and re-reading to check. It has you questioning what you think you know and where nothing is as it seems. Vanessa Thompson is a divorced woman who is barely managing to keep herself together and her days off from her job at Saks endanger her employment. She exists in a alcoholic haze, the wine bottles in her home attest to this. Vanessa used to be married to the wealthy Richard, a good looking hedge fund manager. The end of her marriage has left her floundering as she wonders about the effects of fertility medication, her failure to be the ideal wife, and haunted by events that happened to her when she was at college.<br /><br />What pierces Vanessa's alcoholic haze is the shocking news that Richard is planning to remarry. Something she has no intention of letting happen as she embarks on a crusade. She must protect the intended wife, she must not undergo what Vanesssa suffered. However, is Vanessa to be relied upon? And why should another woman believe her? The narrative is delivered from the perspective of the main characters. This is a story with huge twists and a compelling storyline. It dissects the anatomy and complexities of a marriage, the lies, the secrets, the manipulation and the betrayals. Whilst you may have to occasionally suspend your disbelief, this is nevertheless a book that will grab your attention and never let go. Many thanks to St Martins Press for an ARC.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2153695798" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2153695798" />
    <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters"><img alt="Elyse  Walters" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514246949p2/597461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2153695798?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elyse  Walters" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters">Elyse  Walters</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2153695798" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15310378184001778412">The new *IT* psychological suspense novel - to be released in stores everywhere in January 2018 - is GOOD! It’s really GOOD! <br/><br/>ZERO SPOILERS!!!!!<br/><br/>I personally think it must have been a ‘KICK-OF-FUN’ for authors Greer Hendricks and Sarah Pekkanen to collaborate together. <br/>There is a wonderful YouTube of both authors speaking about ‘how’ they went about writing it together - they didn’t each just take one character. They both worked on everything ..... and it sure sounds like they treasured working to</span>
  <span id="freeText15310378184001778412" style="display:none">The new *IT* psychological suspense novel - to be released in stores everywhere in January 2018 - is GOOD! It’s really GOOD! <br /><br />ZERO SPOILERS!!!!!<br /><br />I personally think it must have been a ‘KICK-OF-FUN’ for authors Greer Hendricks and Sarah Pekkanen to collaborate together. <br />There is a wonderful YouTube of both authors speaking about ‘how’ they went about writing it together - they didn’t each just take one character. They both worked on everything ..... and it sure sounds like they treasured working together. Its very cool to see two women working together like they did: touches something extra special in me. Congrats to them both..... GREAT RESULTS TOO! <br /><br />I’m not going to going to explain this novel away... but you will meet Nellie, Vanessa, Richard, Samantha, Maureen, Charlotte, Mrs Keene, Frank, Lucille, Emma, and a few other characters. <br />Think of ‘all’ the characters in the story - including names I haven’t mentioned as your puzzle pieces. As in doing a jigsaw puzzle, it’s not complete until every piece has been put together. <br />The enjoyment of reading psychological suspense novels, often has more to do with the ‘game’ of piecing the ‘story-puzzle’ together than the specifics of the story itself. <br /><br />As for the storytelling itself - the writing is excellent- the dialogue superb ....with plots and subplots. Some details were more interesting to me than others. For example - I liked there’re being a pre school - “The Learning Ladder” —but rolled my eyes at the cost of $32,000 a year. I wasn’t too crazy about a parent putting her three-year-old in mandarin classes, karate, and music classes all at the same time..... as it feed into my thoughts of “the hurried child”.<br />I’m not thrilled with stereotyping the wealthy parents/ low paying teacher themes in our fiction books too much.... even though I’m aware it’s true. I’m a little tired of it — yet .... I loved the way the characters were developed. <br /><br />The biggest enjoyment was trying to fit clues together and do double takes when surprising chunks fell from the sky. <br />I don’t want my entire reading-diet to be this genre....but when I do pick one —<br />I want the spicy elements of the guessing game to pull the rug out from under me .... <br />“The Wife Between Us” YANKED the rug ( out from under me). <br /><br />4.5 <br /><br />Thank You St. Martin’s Press, Netgalley, Greer Hendricks, and Sarah Pekkhanen<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15310378184001778412" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10015624027015203661"><b>This little number is now available! My favorite thriller of 2017</b><br/><br/><b>WOWOWOWOWOW</b><br/><br/>I am leaving my first impression above because it still fits how I am feeling several hours after finishing this book. I think some may find the first third of this book slower-building (which I happen to love) and possibly even a tiny bit confusing. I will not give anything away, but keep going. Trust me.   <span id="freeText10015624027015203661" style="display:none"><b>This little number is now available! My favorite thriller of 2017</b><br /><br /><b>WOWOWOWOWOW</b><br /><br />I am leaving my first impression above because it still fits how I am feeling several hours after finishing this book. I think some may find the first third of this book slower-building (which I happen to love) and possibly even a tiny bit confusing. I will not give anything away, but keep going. Trust me. I already have a book hangover from this because my next book is not written nearly as well. So about that, the writing is flawless. It flows just how I like. Not an extra word. No fluff, no frills. This was written by two authors, and I have no idea how they did it because it's seamless. <br /><br />The characters- Vanessa, Nellie, Richard, Aunt Charlotte, even Duke- so much to love, hate, and ponder. This had a completely original premise. And the best part- I was duped! <br /><br />The synopsis says it best:<br /><br /><b>Assume nothing.</b><br /><br /> I was floored! My head was spinning. This is a book you will want to discuss with all your book friends once you finish, so please read it and discuss with me! I hope beyond hope that these two authors write together again. Their effort was perfection. <br /><br />Thanks to the authors, the publisher, and Goodreads, for the complimentary copy. This was my honest review. The Wife Between Us will be published January 2018.</span>

<div id="review_2249560002" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2249560002" />
    <a title="Mary Beth " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14233569-mary-beth"><img alt="Mary Beth " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479858526p2/14233569.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2249560002?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary Beth " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary Beth " href="/user/show/14233569-mary-beth">Mary Beth </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2249560002" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15956321304783631728"><br/>I have been sitting on this review for awhile now, thinking on how I want to write it. Each time I started a sentence, I was giving away too much of the plot. I went into this book blindly. I saw that the ratings were awesome and noticed it was a thriller which is my favorite genre, its not only just a thriller but a psychological thriller. I did read the blurb and the blurb didn't give anything away either. I had no idea what this book was about, and this book has lots of twists and turns that </span>
  <span id="freeText15956321304783631728" style="display:none"><br />I have been sitting on this review for awhile now, thinking on how I want to write it. Each time I started a sentence, I was giving away too much of the plot. I went into this book blindly. I saw that the ratings were awesome and noticed it was a thriller which is my favorite genre, its not only just a thriller but a psychological thriller. I did read the blurb and the blurb didn't give anything away either. I had no idea what this book was about, and this book has lots of twists and turns that are full of surprises. The twists and turns make this book so much fun.I suggest you go into this book blindly and hope you get the same surprises as I did. I am using the blurb as my review because I think its perfect for this book, and then I will put down my thoughts.<br /> A novel of suspense that explores the complexities of marriage and the dangerous truths we ignore in the name of love.<br />When you read this book, you will make many assumptions.<br />You will assume you are reading about a jealous wife and her obsession with her replacement.<br />You will assume you are reading about a woman about to enter a new marriage with the man she loves.<br />You will assume the first wife was a disaster and that the husband was well rid of her.<br />You will assume you know the motives, the history, the anatomy of the relationships.<br />Assume nothing.<br /><br />Discover the next blockbuster novel of suspense, and get ready for the read of your life.<br /><br />I can not say that I was hooked straight from the very beginning. This one has a slow burn going into it. Once I got into it though I couldn't put it down. It was like a rollercoaster ride filled with twists and turns. I found this psychological thriller to be very addicting once I got to the suspense. <br /><br />The chapters are very short, so it is a fast paced read. This book is very well written. I loved the dialogue, and the writing style. The characters were so well developed. This one kept me on the edge of my seat and kept me guessing. All the clues were there but it was like a jigsaw puzzle. The pieces of this puzzle just made this an unpredictable read for me. It was so surprising. I could not put it down and kept wondering what was going to happen next. The book ended very well. It kept my attention and amazed me. It has several jaw dropping moments. <br />I recommend it. I want to thank Netgalley, St. Martin's Press and the author for the copy of this book in exchange for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15956321304783631728" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7948278-elaine?shelf=am-i-thrilled">am-i-thrilled</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7948278-elaine?shelf=hot-mess">hot-mess</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7948278-elaine?shelf=first-reads-giveaways">first-reads-giveaways</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7948278-elaine?shelf=fresh-meat">fresh-meat</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7948278-elaine?shelf=punch-n-judy">punch-n-judy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2112402298" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1370771692074146105">I was vaguely optimistic that I might get through 2017 without a rant but lucky me, I won a copy of <b>
  <i>The Wife Between Us</i>
</b> through a Goodreads Giveaway.<br/><br/><i>** Beware of Spoilers and Raging, Wrathful Rant Ahead!!! **</i><br/><br/><b>You have been warned.</b><br/><br/>I actually had to put off writing this review for quite some time until I had cooled down and thought over what I was going to say.<br/><br/><i>Oooh, this is going to be fun. Where shall I begin? (rubbing my hands together with devilish delight)</i><br/><br/>Let's start with our heroine (and I</span>
  <span id="freeText1370771692074146105" style="display:none">I was vaguely optimistic that I might get through 2017 without a rant but lucky me, I won a copy of <b>
  <i>The Wife Between Us</i>
</b> through a Goodreads Giveaway.<br /><br /><i>** Beware of Spoilers and Raging, Wrathful Rant Ahead!!! **</i><br /><br /><b>You have been warned.</b><br /><br />I actually had to put off writing this review for quite some time until I had cooled down and thought over what I was going to say.<br /><br /><i>Oooh, this is going to be fun. Where shall I begin? (rubbing my hands together with devilish delight)</i><br /><br />Let's start with our heroine (and I use this term in the <i>loosest</i> way possible), Vanessa/Nellie, who officially falls into the all popular category of "women who are duped by a handsome, sophisticated man because, well, he's handsome and sophisticated. Do you need more clarification than that?"<br /><br />The first half of the story is told in the voice of Vanessa, her present life as a divorcee, living a sad existence with her widowed artist aunt and earning a meager wage as a retail employee.<br /><br />The second half is told in the voice of Nellie, her previous life just seven years ago, as she was caught in the throes of her whirlwind romance with Richard, a successful businessman. <br /><br />As befitting the archetype in her role as a tragic female character <i>(cue Victorian faint right here)</i>, Vanessa is revealed to be meek and mild (are you really surprised by that?), a preschool teacher with a shameful secret in her past and a mentally unstable mother. <br /><br />Her dark past includes a silly and stereotypical dalliance with a married professor in college. Of course, she gets pregnant and when she goes to tell him she discovers he's married. <i>That cad! He lied!</i><br /><br />You know, this is not the first book I've read in which the main female character slept with her married professor. In this year. <br /><br />Is this the new popular secret employed as a literary device? <br /><br />That doesn't bother me so much as the fact that in this day and age, women are unaware or delusional to the point of not taking care of their sexual health in the forms of contraception and condoms.<br /><br />Unless I'm missing something and all these women went to a school in the Ozarks in which clinics and Planned Parenthood don't exist and they also didn't have sexual education in high school and junior high which explained how sex works?<br /><br />Well, if Trump has his way, we'll all be living in the boonies soon but that's a discussion for another time.<br /><br />Okay, Vanessa falls for Richard, this successful dude whose profession is as much a mystery as what exactly Christian Grey did at Grey Enterprises but hey, what he actually did for a living is of no consequence. <br /><br />What really matters here is that Richard is the epitome of elegance and sophistication, introducing her to expensive food and art and music such as she has never been exposed to. Oh, and he calls her Nellie because he thinks it 'fits' her more and she likes it, <i>tee hee, how sweet, isn't it?</i><br /><br />So what if he is mum about his past and his parents are dead and he doesn't really have any close friends except for a fiercely protective older sister named Maureen?<br /><br />No, that doesn't ring my alarm bells at all.<br /><br /><i>Danger, Vanessa, danger!!!</i><br /><br />Vanessa/Nellie's past and present back and forth recap of events is to draw the reader into her innocent path of how she fell for Richard and her realization that he was not the man she thought him to be <i>(NO WAY!)</i> and her eventual fall from grace, which frankly, I didn't care about because I didn't care about her.<br /><br />The second part details Vanessa's plan to save Richard's next wife, Emma, from a terrible fate, even though (she reveals to the readers) that she had originally planned to get them together in the first place so she could get a divorce.<br /><br />Get it?<br /><br />Wait, it gets better. After escaping from Richard's abusive clutches and engineering Emma into Richard's arms, Vanessa suddenly realizes "Wow, what did I just do? I managed to escape a wife beater by getting an innocent woman to take my place. Damn, I'm so clever but now I have to save her life because I couldn't think of a more plausible plan, like accidentally killing him or something more interesting."<br /><br />Vanessa is unable to convince Emma of Richard's true nature because Richard has easily convinced everyone, including Emma, that Vanessa is crazy. <br /><br />Yup, the always popular standby of <i>my-ex-wife-is-crazy-and-obsessive-and-forgets-to-do-stuff-because-her-mother-is-mentally-ill-ploy</i> is being used here, the third (or fourth) time I've read in a novel, so far, this year, that I can remember.<br /><br />As a result of her lack of credibility, Vanessa devises an ingenious plan to prove to Emma that Richard is dangerous by staging a confrontation with Richard in the hopes that he will strike her and Emma will see for herself what Richard truly is.<br /><br /><i>Holy shit, this is a great plan.</i> All domestic abusive survivors should try this in case people don't believe they are being abused and can't receive help or support.<br /><br />Not only do I have to contend with sexual violence as a literary device in movies, television and novels, I now have to deal with the ongoing trend where authors use mental illness as a literary device in which to break down an already weak and pathetic character and why she can't be trusted.<br /><br /><i>When in doubt, call her 'mentally ill!'</i><br /><br />You still with me? We still have a way to go.<br /><br />To recap, there is nothing original in <b>
  <i>The Wife Between Us</i>
</b> filled with lackluster characters, a marriage built on 'secrets' and 'lies' and ‘obfuscation' and the women who bed these <b>adulterous</b> a**holes because they don't love themselves.<br /><br />But that doesn't make me mad.<br /><br />I'll tell you what makes me furious about this book.<br /><br />When Richard's sister, Maureen, justifies his degrading behavior by explaining that their father had abused and mistreated their mother.<br /><br />Oh, is that all? <br /><br /><b>Well, why didn't you say so? All is forgiven!</b><br /><br />Let no one be held accountable in this world. <br /><br />All rapists, pedophiles, pervs, adulterers, animal abusers, murderers, listen up: if you had a terrible childhood and saw horrible things, it's okay. You are not held responsible for the atrocious deeds you will later commit because you are not to blame. Your parents are to blame! The horrid events you witness are to blame! Not you! You all had bad childhoods!<br /><br />You are all absolved! Go forth and continue to rape, murder, mutilate, maim, harm, torture and destroy to your heart's content.<br /><br />OMFG, are you kidding me? <br /><br /><i>(At this point, I actually had to put the book down, partly because I didn't know whether to start cursing or start laughing at this simple, pathetic excuse to exonerate a man for his disgusting actions.)</i><br /><br />You know, I could ignore the one dimensional, unremarkable and unforgettable Nellie, the boring exposition of her life and the trivial and demeaning stereotypes of domestic abuse survivors. I could even bypass the unoriginal plot and the boring drone of the stiff writing style.<br /><br />I could even overlook the unbelievable, dumb-ass, <b>HILARIOUS</b> twist of the ending when it is revealed that Emma is the daughter of the professor Vanessa had an affair with and Emma's goal in life was to ruin the woman who ruined her parents' marriage. I noticed she blamed Vanessa for the failure of her parents' marriage and not her father's wandering dick.<br /><br />Jeez, Freud was right. Everyone has daddy issues, not just in real life.<br /><br />But I can't overlook the fact that this novel was written by not just one woman, but two! And in their world, men will be men and women will be...well, sad sacks lacking strength, individuality and redeeming qualities.<br /><br />The back copy of the book says:<br /><br /><i>When you read this book, you will make assumptions. Assume nothing.</i><br /><br />I agree. This book is <b>
  <i>nothing.</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1370771692074146105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2124354452" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2124354452" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2124354452?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=mystery-shelf">mystery-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2124354452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14390337914375256895">The Wife Between Us is a 2017 St. Martin’s Press publication. <br/><br/>Engrossing domestic thriller! <br/><br/>This book got such a tremendous response from my fellow GR friends, I shot it up to the top of my TBR list, ignoring my usual cautionary optimistic approach to well received popular books, because I just had a feeling this one would deliver. <br/><br/><br/>Richard’s first wife, Vanessa, was dumped for a younger woman after many years of marriage. Gone were all the trappings of wealth she had enjoyed as she struggles to </span>
  <span id="freeText14390337914375256895" style="display:none">The Wife Between Us is a 2017 St. Martin’s Press publication. <br /><br />Engrossing domestic thriller! <br /><br />This book got such a tremendous response from my fellow GR friends, I shot it up to the top of my TBR list, ignoring my usual cautionary optimistic approach to well received popular books, because I just had a feeling this one would deliver. <br /><br /><br />Richard’s first wife, Vanessa, was dumped for a younger woman after many years of marriage. Gone were all the trappings of wealth she had enjoyed as she struggles to put her life back in order. <br /><br />Forced to live with her aunt and take a job at Saks, Vanessa’s thinks obsessively about Richard’s new girlfriend, Nellie, while consuming large quantities of alcohol. When she inadvertently finds out that Richard plans to remarry, her fragile state of mind spirals out of control. The only thing she can think about is confronting Nellie for a face to face showdown. <br /><br />Nellie, by all appearances, seems like a sweet girl, perhaps a bit naïve, completely smitten with her fiancé, Richard. She can’t wait to start her new, ‘dream come true' life with her dashing, successful husband. But, she, too, may have a few dark secrets lurking in her past. But, unbeknownst to Nellie, she is being watched, even stalked by a woman whose driving force in life is to prevent her wedding from ever taking place. <br /><br />The author did a fantastic job of doling out just the right amount of information at key intervals, subtly changing the dynamics of the story by giving the reader another possible angle to explore. <br /><br />My initial impressions of the situation presented to me, morphs little by little, as pieces of the puzzle are slowly revealed. Once the entire jigsaw puzzle is complete, the picture staring back at me, looks nothing at all like what I was expecting. <br /><br /><br />This story has a few surprises I never saw coming. The only minor let down was that the plot had a few similarities to another book I’d read just a few weeks ago, which deflated the balloon a little, but not too much, because it didn’t become obvious until I was already very deep into the book. <br /><br />The truth is, the author kept me guessing and on my toes pretty much from start to finish. I was a bit conflicted about the final turn of the screw. I usually love all that added relish on top, but lately those late minute plot twists are becoming all too common, making them more tiresome than anything else and falling flat, as a result. In this case, the story could have ended quite satisfactorily without that final revelation, but I suppose, since it was a complete shock to me, I must grudgingly concede my approval for sneaking that one by me completely undetected. <br /><br />Overall, I’m not sure I was as blown away by this one as my contemporaries, but this is a very solid, highly entertaining domestic thriller, and is certainly worth checking out. <br /><br />4 stars<br /><br />*Netgalley</span>
  <a data-text-id="14390337914375256895" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2567477720895524961">I am just speechless! <br/><br/>There are so many twists, I was seeing double! My head was spinning and I went back to re-read several parts to “make sure” I read what I thought I read. Yes, that is exactly what I read. She is young and pretty just like her former self and Vanessa is having a hard time dealing with reality! Richard is the handsome, but</span>
  <span id="freeText2567477720895524961" style="display:none">I am just speechless! <br /><br />There are so many twists, I was seeing double! My head was spinning and I went back to re-read several parts to “make sure” I read what I thought I read. Yes, that is exactly what I read. I need a lifeline….can I call a friend?<br /><br />Meet Vanessa, the ex-wife with issues. I think I know her! She is jealous and obsessed with her replacement, Nellie. She is young and pretty just like her former self and Vanessa is having a hard time dealing with reality! Richard is the handsome, but controlling husband. What are Richard's motives?<br /><br />Vanessa is determined to stop Richard’s marriage from happening and nothing will stop her.<br /><br />Even if your detective skills are top-notch, you will be hood-winked. Enjoy!<br /><br />My stop on the blog tour will be on December 6, 2017 at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://dressedtoread.com/">https://dressedtoread.com/</a><br />Thank you to St.Martin's Press for my ARC.</span>
