<div id="review_2257171278" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2257171278" />
    <a title="Evgnossia O&#39;Hara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43416866-evgnossia-o-hara"><img alt="Evgnossia O&#39;Hara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537347712p2/43416866.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2257171278?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgnossia O&#39;Hara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgnossia O&#39;Hara" href="/user/show/43416866-evgnossia-o-hara">Evgnossia O&#39;Hara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43416866-evgnossia-o-hara?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43416866-evgnossia-o-hara?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2257171278" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer173752682316282474">Review was originally published on <a href='https://throughthechapters.wordpress.com/2018/01/29/the-wife-between-us-by-greer-hendricks-sarah-pekkanenreview/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Through the Chapters|Blog</a><br/><br/><b>*3 stars*</b><br/><br/>Have you heard about the ironic process theory which deals with the attempts to suppress certain thoughts and by this means make them more likely to surface?<br/><br/>For example, imagine a situation where someone tells you not to think about pink elephants. So, what are you doing? You are thinking about those pink elephants. You picture them in your mind in all their glory and even when you try to think of something else they invade int</span>
  <span id="freeText173752682316282474" style="display:none">Review was originally published on <a href="https://throughthechapters.wordpress.com/2018/01/29/the-wife-between-us-by-greer-hendricks-sarah-pekkanenreview/" rel="nofollow noopener">Through the Chapters|Blog</a><br><br><b>*3 stars*</b><br><br>Have you heard about the ironic process theory which deals with the attempts to suppress certain thoughts and by this means make them more likely to surface?<br><br>For example, imagine a situation where someone tells you not to think about pink elephants. So, what are you doing? You are thinking about those pink elephants. You picture them in your mind in all their glory and even when you try to think of something else they invade into your thoughts again. Ironic, isn’t it?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517226633ra/24959129.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>So, when I’ve read the synopsis of “The Wife Between Us” and have been warned to<br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>Assume nothing</blockquote>
  </b>
</i> <br>What did I do? I was assuming, I was wondering, I was guessing, non-stop, throughout the story. Guess what. I figured out the first plot twist which had to blow my mind away. But it just didn’t happen since I was warned to assume nothing. See? The ironic process theory.<br><br>Let’s put first things firsts. I was craving to read this book the first time I saw it on Goodreads. The cover was intriguing; the reception of my Goodreads friends astonishing, and the synopsis made me assuming theories even before I had the change to read the first line.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517226633ra/24959127.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Generally speaking, the story deals with two young women, an ex-wife and a bride to be. Vanessa and Nellie. They both are in love with Richard, an accomplished man who can protect the woman of his life. Vanessa, the jealous ex-wife, is not ready to let him continue with his life and marry Nellie. As a result, she’s trying to prevent this marriage no matter the cost and the consequences. I won’t tell something else on the plot as I don’t want to spoil you. You’d better go into it, knowing as less as possible.<br><br>To continue with my reading experience, some may thing that the first part of the story was a little bit dragged but it was essential for the writers to construct the background of the main characters and lead to the main plot twist. The same plot twist that I figured out in the early stage of my reading. Needless to say, I was disappointed; I didn’t have the chance to feel this turmoil that good turns of events produce.<br><br>Nonetheless, I was still yearning for the development of the story and was waiting for the next plot twist in order to compensate myself. I have to confess that some lines in the novel such as…<br><i>
  <blockquote>I never been the woman he thought he’d married.</blockquote>
</i><br>and…<br><i>
  <blockquote>They say the wife is always the last to know.</blockquote>
</i><br>…made me eager to keep reading, to keep turning the pages, just to learn what happens next, where the story will lead me, but at the same time I was assuming again. And again I was somehow right. What is the problem with me?<br><br>Still, I was waiting for the great plot twist until the very last page, till the very last sentence. Unfortunately, I wasn’t struck with amazement. There were another one plot twist but I was completely uninterested in that one. To tell more, it was unnecessary as it didn’t change anything in my already thorough opinion. The only thing I wanted to do was:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517226633ra/24959128.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I have to acknowledge some positive aspects of the novel. The writing was flawless; the characters were multidimensional with past and secrets that made me to continue reading. It was a generator of controversial emotions. I felt compassion, anger, happiness and even malice. I cannot also omit the message that the story provides us with. You will understand after reading the book.<br><br><i>
  <blockquote>
    <p>That’s why I love reading. A book is not only a good story or a shocking plot twist; it is a journey, a message, a lesson, a life, a powerful and deep gift which speaks a different truth to each and every one of us.</p>
  </blockquote>
</i><br>With those in mind, if you decide to read “The Wife Between Us”, do not stay at the “assume nothing”, cause you will activate your mind to assume everything and in all likelihood to guess the main twist or a part of it. But if we’ll take under consideration the theory, you have already arguably aroused your mind to assume, guess and judge. So, I’m the one to blame here…<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1513778869ra/24721856.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="173752682316282474" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1992212234" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1992212234" />
    <a title="Mischenko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko"><img alt="Mischenko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587209348p2/1194517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1992212234?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mischenko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mischenko" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko">Mischenko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35494553-the-wife-between-us">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1194517-mischenko?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1194517-mischenko?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1992212234" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17553002158699081700">This review can be seen @ <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://readrantrockandroll.com/2017/12/12/the-wife-between-us-by-greer-hendricks-and-sarah-pekkanen-book-review/'>https://readrantrockandroll.com/2017/...</a><br/><br/>Vanessa has problems. Now that she’s divorced from Richard, she can’t stand the fact that Richard has moved on. Not only is he his usual thriving self, but now he’s getting married to someone new–someone young and beautiful. It just so happens that this new woman reminds Vanessa of someone she used to be.<br/><br/>What is it about Richard? Was he a perfect husband? Is he truly a knight in shining armor? Was Vanessa a psycho and mentally uns</span>
  <span id="freeText17553002158699081700" style="display:none">This review can be seen @ <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://readrantrockandroll.com/2017/12/12/the-wife-between-us-by-greer-hendricks-and-sarah-pekkanen-book-review/">https://readrantrockandroll.com/2017/...</a><br /><br />Vanessa has problems. Now that she’s divorced from Richard, she can’t stand the fact that Richard has moved on. Not only is he his usual thriving self, but now he’s getting married to someone new–someone young and beautiful. It just so happens that this new woman reminds Vanessa of someone she used to be.<br /><br />What is it about Richard? Was he a perfect husband? Is he truly a knight in shining armor? Was Vanessa a psycho and mentally unstable wife? Who’s to blame for the marriage ending and what role do the others have in this story?<br /><br />I went in to this book super excited after reading multiple rave reviews about it from friends on Goodreads. It seemed like everyone was loving it, so I went straight to NetGalley and put in my request. After I started reading it, I didn’t want to put it down. I thought for sure I knew where the story was going. It felt slow to me, but I hung on until nearly halfway through when the first major twist was introduced. I was shocked! I was so very surprised and befuddled thinking that I’d skipped something or that I was lost. It seemed unique and interesting, but as time went on, I became disentranced and my mind began to wonder away from the story. The characters became confusing to me and the plot felt all over the place. It was like I wanted to get to the ending to see how things would unfold, but there simply wasn’t anything going on to captivate me. At times, I felt like there was too much information and in other places, simply not enough. I didn’t feel like it was horribly predictable as there were plenty of twists and a strange reveal at the end, but even with all the crazy twists, this just ended up being an okay read for me and it just didn’t feel like a thriller.<br /><br />I did still enjoy it and feel like this is going to be a favorite for many people! I will still recommend this because I know many will love it. The title, cover, and blurb fit the story perfectly!<br /><br />Thanks to Netgalley for this ARC of <i>The Wife Between Us.</i><br /><br />3***</span>
  <a data-text-id="17553002158699081700" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11514592354361608412">4.5*<br/>When a book can create a buzz…when my sense of anxiety notches up! I know I’ve come across a great read! <br/>This fantastic new release by Greer Hendricks and Sarah Pekkanen did just that for me! With a constant aura of anticipation and unease, (Just what we love when reading a thriller!) I breezed through the pages. <br/><br/>I was reminded partially through, (thank you Brenda!) that a wicked twist lay ahead. Yet even with a heads-up, I never saw it coming! <b>Whaaat??!!</b> And bonus…there were plenty more to </span>
  <span id="freeText11514592354361608412" style="display:none">4.5*<br />When a book can create a buzz…when my sense of anxiety notches up! I know I’ve come across a great read! <br />This fantastic new release by Greer Hendricks and Sarah Pekkanen did just that for me! With a constant aura of anticipation and unease, (Just what we love when reading a thriller!) I breezed through the pages. <br /><br />I was reminded partially through, (thank you Brenda!) that a wicked twist lay ahead. Yet even with a heads-up, I never saw it coming! <b>Whaaat??!!</b> And bonus…there were plenty more to come! <br /><br />A fantastic, mind-bending thriller dealing with… marriage, divorce and the other woman (not necessarily in that order!). And well, I’ll just stop there! I won’t keep rattling on and risk giving anything away. Trust me, the less you know going in, the more you’ll enjoy this one!<br />And be forewarned – you’ll want to clear your schedule. Once you start, you won’t want to put this one down! A great collaboration from Ms. Hendricks and Ms. Pekkanen. An exciting new writing duo in the thriller arena. Can’t wait for their next release!!<br /><br />A wonderful Traveling Sister Read with Brenda, Norma, Lindsay and Susanne!<br /><br />Thank you to NetGalley, St. Martin’s Press and Greer Hendricks and Sarah Pekkanen for an ARC of this novel to read and review.<br /><br />For this review and our Full Traveling Sister review please visit Norma and Brenda’s fabulous book blog: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.twogirlslostinacouleereading.wordpress.com">http://www.twogirlslostinacouleereadi...</a><br /></span>

<div id="review_2155000751" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2155000751" />
    <a title="Debbie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8665845-debbie"><img alt="Debbie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334166735p2/8665845.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2155000751?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie" href="/user/show/8665845-debbie">Debbie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=omg-twists">omg-twists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=runners-up-2012-through-2019">runners-up-2012-through-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=debuts">debuts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=new-york-city">new-york-city</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=complicated-female-relationships">complicated-female-relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=favorite-thrillers">favorite-thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2155000751" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5292019940664205621"><b>EEK! A twister blister</b> formed in my poor brain and it was ready to burst! This thriller had a twist that made me think three things, explanations that jumped fast around inside my head, irritating the hell out of the blister: Either I was an absolute dummy, or I had meandered into the Twilight Zone, or the publisher (or editor) had made a mistake that was mammoth and unforgiveable. <br/><br/><b>My 10-step journey:</b><br/><br/>1. <b>Was going along just fine,</b> enjoying this fast-moving thriller. La-dee-da, la-dee-da. <br/><br/>2. <b>Got h</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5292019940664205621" style="display:none"><b>EEK! A twister blister</b> formed in my poor brain and it was ready to burst! This thriller had a twist that made me think three things, explanations that jumped fast around inside my head, irritating the hell out of the blister: Either I was an absolute dummy, or I had meandered into the Twilight Zone, or the publisher (or editor) had made a mistake that was mammoth and unforgiveable. <br /><br /><b>My 10-step journey:</b><br /><br />1. <b>Was going along just fine,</b> enjoying this fast-moving thriller. La-dee-da, la-dee-da. <br /><br />2. <b>Got hit. WHAP!</b> What just happened???? I was about halfway through. Surely all will be made clear in a second. But it wasn’t. I should understand. But I don’t. Way too confusing!<br /><br />3. <b>Reread pages.</b> At first, I did so patiently, though nervously. Nothing clicked. A book should not be this hard! <br /><br />4. <b>Reread the pages a few dozen more times.</b> I kept at it. Reread these sentences, carefully, I told myself, they WILL make sense. They always do in the end. But I was losing my dear patience. I was mad, I tell you. How could they do this to me? Despite my attempt at soothing self-talk, this book continued to make NO sense.<br /><br />5. <b>Paced.</b> Okay, I’m a sitter, not a pacer. For this sitter to actually pace in the middle of reading a book is an unheard-of event. I usually just sit still and let my head (instead of my legs) do the work. As I clomped through my all-in-a-row living room, dining room, and kitchen (a nice straight place to pace), I tried desperately to figure out what was going on in this book that had hooked me from the start. I had pretty much settled on the idea that of the three possibilities, I was a dummy, unfit to handle a twist in a stupid book (because by this time, I was defensively calling the book “stupid”).<br /><br />6. <b>Paced some more.</b> I don’t remember it clearly (due to stress, which often obliterates memory), but I’m pretty sure I was cussing by this point. I should have been wearing a pedometer.<br /><br />7. <b>Loaded the dishwasher.</b> The hell with this book, I’ll do my chores. Doing the dishes never seemed so pleasant.<br /><br />8. <b>Sat back down.</b> Should I abandon this book? Throw my Kindle across the room? (Not a smart idea to throw an electronic device, so I nixed it.) I was really pissed off. A book should not make me this mad or be this hard. My head hurt. Maybe I should call a friend and just forget about this dumb story.<br /><br />9. <b>Reread pages one last time.</b> Okay, I’ll try, but that’s it—no more. <br /><br />10. <b>And then….OMG, I get it!!!!</b> I get it!!!! I love this book! This twist is genius!! I felt like I had found the last piece in a 3,000-piece jigsaw puzzle. I was all cocky now that I had finally understood, and I could not stop marveling at the ingenuity of it. The authors winked at me. I winked back.<br /><br />So that was my frustrating journey. I was exhausted, both mentally and physically. But then I started reading like a mad fool; my energy was renewed. Plus my dishes were done and I had had a little exercise. <br /><br />It’s about time that I mentioned what the book is about: A scorned, obsessed ex-wife whose ex-husband is about marry again, is stalking the new fiancé. There are some good secrets about everyone’s past. As I read on, though, I realized that no twist could outdo that first one. That first humdinger was a twist of a different kind, but I’m not going to elaborate. I don’t want to give anything away.<br /><br />The twists continued. What fun to have a stream of them, not just one. Most books don’t come with a variety. I could not stop reading. In fact, I read this book in two days, which is super fast for me. <br /><br />But yes, there was a bit of a letdown, only because that first twist was so grand. Also, the characters were somewhat stereotypical at first. Even some of the twists seemed a little familiar. But there were surprises that were new. The Epilogue was really good, for instance. Really good.<br /><br />I do think this book might be a blockbuster. Unlike in Gone Girl, however, the language didn’t slay me; it was pretty pedestrian. I liked that there were no wasted words, though. As an ex-editor, I’m fascinated by the fact that this was written by two people. I can’t imagine how that worked.<br /><br />This book is being brought to the big screen. I can’t for the life of me figure out how that first twist will be handled—sure hope they don’t have to ditch it, because the movie wouldn’t be as great without it. I’m definitely lining up to see the movie, though. <br /><br />I recommend this book because of all the twists. As the blurb says, assume nothing, because nothing, and I mean nothing, is as it seems. I definitely thought it was a lot of fun, despite the pain of my twister blister. <br /><br />Thanks to NetGalley for the advance copy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5292019940664205621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2173930773" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15679152577109877664">Just a few more days to enter my giveaway!<b>GIVEAWAY</b>💙 12/15/17 - I have not one, not two but THREE copies of The Wife Between Us to giveaway! You can enter on my blog <a href='https://thebookcollective.net/2017/12/15/giveaway-three-copies-of-the-wife-between-us/' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a> .<br/><br/>____________<br/><br/>Engrossing and addictive, this little gem of a thriller with a major twist had me second guessing every character and I loved every moment of it!<br/><br/>This is one of those books that is unputdownable – you will be thinking of the characters when you’re not reading and wondering how it will all pan out. I had absolutely no</span>
  <span id="freeText15679152577109877664" style="display:none">Just a few more days to enter my giveaway!<b>GIVEAWAY</b>💙 12/15/17 - I have not one, not two but THREE copies of The Wife Between Us to giveaway! You can enter on my blog <a href="https://thebookcollective.net/2017/12/15/giveaway-three-copies-of-the-wife-between-us/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> .<br /><br />____________<br /><br />Engrossing and addictive, this little gem of a thriller with a major twist had me second guessing every character and I loved every moment of it!<br /><br />This is one of those books that is unputdownable – you will be thinking of the characters when you’re not reading and wondering how it will all pan out. I had absolutely no idea who to trust throughout the story, my opinion changed every chapter. This was a deeply intricate plot and all the pieces came together perfectly in the end.<br /><br />I wasn’t sure how a book written by two authors would work out, but they managed to seamlessly tell this tale. This is a well written, fast-paced story that will keep you guessing all the way to the epilogue. Fans of the psychological thriller – you don’t want to miss this one!<br /><br />You can also find my review on my blog for the blog tour at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.thebookcollective.net">www.thebookcollective.net</a>.<br /><br />Thank you to Netgalley, Greer Hendricks, Sarah Pakkanen and St. Martin’s press for a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review.</span>

  <span id="freeText3514852328456101809" style="display:none">okay. its official - im creating a new genre. i dont feel like this falls under thriller or mystery. this is pure psychological domestic D R A M A and i am here for it. <br /><br />the book blurb for this is very vague and i think that suits the story perfectly. the narrator is unreliable (ugh. i hate the <i>‘alcoholic ex’</i> trope, but whatever. i could deal with it in this), everyone talks in half truths, and the way the story is told is twisty turvy. yes, that does add some thrilling/mysterious elements, but thats not the heart of this story. its about a husband and wife and what happens in/to their marriage. <br /><br />i will admit the story itself isnt the most original, but its the cleverness in how it is told that really hooked me. there is a lot of misdirection that totally caught me off guard in a couple of places. like i said, nothing really thrilling or mysterious, but very clever and i can appreciate that. <br /><br />i am looking forward to picking up more books by these two ladies!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_2186589985" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2186589985" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2186589985?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5872506-larry-h?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2186589985" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17690986975646945193">I'm between 3 and 3.5 stars. Maybe 3.25?<br/><br/>"In my marriage, there were three truths, three alternate and sometimes compelling realities. There was Richard's truth. There was my truth. And there was the actual truth, which is always the most elusive to recognize. This could be the case in every relationship that we think we've entered into a union with another person when, in fact, we've formed a triangle with one point anchored by a silent but all-seeing judge, the arbiter of reality."<br/><br/>Vanessa's mar</span>
  <span id="freeText17690986975646945193" style="display:none">I'm between 3 and 3.5 stars. Maybe 3.25?<br /><br />"In my marriage, there were three truths, three alternate and sometimes compelling realities. There was Richard's truth. There was my truth. And there was the actual truth, which is always the most elusive to recognize. This could be the case in every relationship that we think we've entered into a union with another person when, in fact, we've formed a triangle with one point anchored by a silent but all-seeing judge, the arbiter of reality."<br /><br />Vanessa's marriage is over. She once had a handsome, rich, powerful husband, and they lived a life of luxury. But they drifted apart, and her husband found another woman. Now she lives with her aunt, wears out-of-date clothing, and is a shell of herself, working a job she hates just to make ends meet.<br /><br />Nellie is a bubbly, young, beautiful preschool teacher. She's finally met her Prince Charming, the man who will rescue her from her messy shared apartment, her nights spent as a cocktail waitress (even though she enjoys them), and takeout meals before hanging out with her friends at various bars and clubs. She also has secrets of her own, and things that cause her to be afraid, and she hopes her fiancé will save her from those, too.<br /><br />If you think <b>
  <i>The Wife Between Us</i>
</b> is a story about a jilted wife jealous of her husband's new fiancée, you're not quite right. This is a story about how things are seldom as simple as they seem, and how appearances can be deceiving. It's also a story about trust, fear, truth, manipulation, and finding your own way.<br /><br />Greer Hendricks and Sarah Pekkanen throw a lot of twists into this book, which is why my description is fairly spartan, because I don't want to spoil anything for you. Every time you think you have things figured out, they swerve again, so you definitely want to keep reading, to see where it all winds up.<br /><br />There are a lot of thrillers out there these days, and many of them deal with relationships that don't go as planned, and the aftermath of breakups, as well as the manipulation that often occurs within a relationship. While the twists definitely jolted the plot a bit, overall I felt a lot of the plotlines were very familiar. At times, I found myself growing a little impatient with the pace of the story, because I wanted to see where Hendricks and Pekkanen would go next, and wanted to move past some of the more commonplace incidents.<br /><br />Is this a compelling thriller? It definitely has its moments, and many of my Goodreads friends have raved about this, so maybe I've just read too many books in this genre this year. It did keep me guessing, though, and sometimes I was right, and sometimes I was wrong. This will probably be one of the beach reads of 2018, so don't let me dissuade you from picking it up.<br /><br />NetGalley and St. Martin's Press provided me an advance copy of the book in exchange for an unbiased review. Thanks for making this available! <br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com">http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blo...</a>.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9472704-linda?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2099783133" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17100733504388500756">Piercing eyes locked in.......trying to make sense of what has just transpired.<br/><br/>Like the unsettled feeling of reclaiming your own wine glass in a sea of abandoned stemware left willy nilly on a crowded bar. A second's turn of your back and your identity is gone. Claimed by another or still existing in a look-alike world. Here and then gone......<br/><br/>Vanessa Thompson awakens in the tiny guestroom in her Aunt Charlotte's apartment. Her marriage is over and the aftermath is like shattered glass with the </span>
  <span id="freeText17100733504388500756" style="display:none">Piercing eyes locked in.......trying to make sense of what has just transpired.<br /><br />Like the unsettled feeling of reclaiming your own wine glass in a sea of abandoned stemware left willy nilly on a crowded bar. A second's turn of your back and your identity is gone. Claimed by another or still existing in a look-alike world. Here and then gone......<br /><br />Vanessa Thompson awakens in the tiny guestroom in her Aunt Charlotte's apartment. Her marriage is over and the aftermath is like shattered glass with the pieces of her remaining life never quite fitting together again. Examining the fragments will only initiate the bleeding once more. A promise of retrieving the hidden wine bottles in her closet at the end of the day gives her the impetus to dress for her retail job at Saks. She also walks a tightrope there with impending dismissal looming because of her constant days off.<br /><br />Richard had all the fine cut and polish of the successful man on the cover of GQ. His position as a hedge fund manager brought them the finer things in life. What could possibly go wrong with perfection? Vanessa asks herself if her skittish behavior was due to the fertility medications she was taking after constant unsuccessful episodes. Was it the fear of retribution from a horrendous haunting situation that occured in her senior year of college? Or was it simply that wine glass that beckoned to be constantly refilled?<br /><br />Startling news drifts in Vanessa's direction as the realization comes that Richard is to be remarried soon. One thing that Vanessa knows for sure is that that is not going to happen. Weak in mind, heart, and spirit, Vanessa is determined to get Richard's attention. One way or another.<br /><br />Greer Hendricks and Sarah Pekkanen present a storyline carved out with mega twists and turns. The eyes tend to deceive in this one. I mean, really deceive. That lipstick smudge on that wine glass may not actually be yours. Then where is yours and where is theirs? Guess you're going to have to crack this one open to see for yourself. Told in three main parts, you'll be flipping back pages to knock on reality's door. Did that just happen? Yep, yep it did......<br /><br />I received an advanced copy of The Wife Between Us through St. Martin's Press. My thanks to them and to Greer Hendricks and Sarah Pekkanen for the opportunity.</span>

    <a title="Charlotte May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may"><img alt="Charlotte May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596906925p2/14002983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2711358990?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte May" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may">Charlotte May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781509842834" href="/book/show/38913614-the-wife-between-us">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=contemporary-recent">contemporary-recent</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=crime-mystery-thriller">crime-mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=illness-mental-terminal">illness-mental-terminal</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2711358990" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4236422567427832654">That was good!!!<br/><br/><i> "I'm not afraid of storms, for I'm learning to sail my ship." </i><br/><br/>I love it when a book can make you think one thing and then pull a 180. You're reading along, minding your own business certain you know what and who you are reading about when suddenly the rug is pulled out from under you and you realise you knew nothing Jon Snow.<br/><br/>Part 1 has 2 POVs. The 27 year old nursery school teacher about to marry the rich, handsome and charming man of her dreams, and the ex wife; shunned and poo</span>
  <span id="freeText4236422567427832654" style="display:none">That was good!!!<br /><br /><i> "I'm not afraid of storms, for I'm learning to sail my ship." </i><br /><br />I love it when a book can make you think one thing and then pull a 180. You're reading along, minding your own business certain you know what and who you are reading about when suddenly the rug is pulled out from under you and you realise you knew nothing Jon Snow.<br /><br />Part 1 has 2 POVs. The 27 year old nursery school teacher about to marry the rich, handsome and charming man of her dreams, and the ex wife; shunned and poor reeling from the shock of her marriage's abrupt end.<br /><br />Vanessa is determined to stop Richard's marriage to the woman she see as 'her replacement', who was also conveniently Richard's PA (oh the cliches!). She comes across as unstable, broken and grief stricken. From the offset it seems like the usual jilted ex hating on the other woman.<br /><br />HOWEVER. There is so much more to this story than that. Dw I won't spoil anything, just know that what you think is or isn't happening WILL BE WRONG.<br /><br />Greer and Sarah did a great job of keeping me hooked right from the get go. There was this underlying anxiety and tension that just kept me turning the pages.<br /><br />And the final little twist at the end sealed the deal for me :) <br /><br />If you enjoy a good thriller then don't miss this one!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4236422567427832654" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ymhCHG1Gm4q+p5ViLUhiJByz5/QwP9RMapJ9BxlmBmhr7ii0aNeWk/iemXQ9XGgTbJ7hTobiDmU+ssA1d/bnBA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('L4wSEEhmG4a0Itr3gIq5xjvXEQVGivBWJeDjRxlCKN+OCni4TfcWn/Ib1uGQnrPxS/oXv/BXKn9xwF51d9LJsw==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer15547474198482210100">Greer Hendricks and Sarah Pekkanen are the co-authors of the blockbuster New York Times bestseller, THE WIFE BETWEEN US, as well as the forthcoming, AN ANONYMOUS GIRL. AN ANONYMOUS GIRL has been optioned for a television series by eOne, with Sarah and Greer executive producing. THE WIFE BETWEEN US has been optioned for film by Amblin Entertainment, with Sarah and Greer screenwriting the adaptation</span>
  <span id="freeText15547474198482210100" style="display:none">Greer Hendricks and Sarah Pekkanen are the co-authors of the blockbuster New York Times bestseller, THE WIFE BETWEEN US, as well as the forthcoming, AN ANONYMOUS GIRL. AN ANONYMOUS GIRL has been optioned for a television series by eOne, with Sarah and Greer executive producing. THE WIFE BETWEEN US has been optioned for film by Amblin Entertainment, with Sarah and Greer screenwriting the adaptation.</span>
